  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_8a2da00b-2d6d-49ce-b741-866261109c51'
      });
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer1749162341190929263"><b>Hunter. Autumn. Summer.<br/>Different homes. Different guardians. Different last names.<br/>Different lives.<br/>But there is one person who binds them together.<br/><i>Kristina</i>.</b><br/><br/>Nineteen years after Kristina Snow met the monster---crank---her children are reeling from the consequences of her decisions.   <span id="freeText1749162341190929263" style="display:none"><b>Hunter. Autumn. Summer.<br />Different homes. Different guardians. Different last names.<br />Different lives.<br />But there is one person who binds them together.<br /><i>Kristina</i>.</b><br /><br />Nineteen years after Kristina Snow met the monster---crank---her children are reeling from the consequences of her decisions. Instead of one big, happy family, they are a desperate tangle of scattered lives united by anger, doubt, and fear.<br /><br />A predisposition to addiction and a sense of emptiness where a mother's love should be leads all three down the road of their mother's notorious legacy. Sex, drugs, alcohol, abuse---there is more of Kristina in her children than they would ever like to believe. But when the thread that ties them together brings them face-to-face, they'll discover something powerful in each other and in themselves---the trust, the hope, the courage to begin to break the cycle.<br /><br /><i>Fallout</i> is bestselling author Ellen Hopkin's riveting conclusion to her trilogy begun by <i>Crank</i> and <i>Glass</i>. It is a revelation and a testament to the harsh reality that addiction is never just one person's problem.</span>

<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/62059254-sydd-robinson">Sydd Robinson</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">It's purposely left feeling unwrapped because a) it's based off her daughter's real continuous life, and b) after she wrote this book the daughter got<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">It's purposely left feeling unwrapped because a) it's based off her daughter's real continuous life, and b) after she wrote this book the daughter got serious about recovery and Hopkins didn't want to trigger a relapse by continuing the story. A lot of her books end like this with more to be desired though a lot of the books (i think its Perfect that mentions Hunter) have little easter eggs to other characters and their journeys from the Crank series .<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">No. To read this, one needs good reading skills AND a good grasp of English. <br/><br/>There are reviews written by English speakers who are frustrated in tryin<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">No. To read this, one needs good reading skills AND a good grasp of English. <br /><br />There are reviews written by English speakers who are frustrated in trying to read this book. I don't understand this issue by English speakers, but there it is. Many English speakers cannot decipher the lines in these books. Since I don't have this issue, I can't understand it, actually. But there is no denying there are many reviews by English readers who can't seem to understand or follow the plot.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_859486570" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/859486570" />
    <a title="Giselle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle"><img alt="Giselle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1310159877p2/4800103.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/859486570?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Giselle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Giselle" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle">Giselle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781442471801" href="/book/show/15801340-fallout">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer859486570" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14825958654342816179">I think I personally enjoyed book 1 and 2 the most, but this one was incredibly powerful. Told in the perspective of Kristina's children almost 20 years later, Fallout shows us not only the long term effects of addiction, but also how wide the effects go. How many people and generation it touches. How many lives it marks. These kids all have deep rooted psychological issues caused by the simple fact of being born by an addict, but also by being abandoned, feeling unloved and alone. It was intere</span>
  <span id="freeText14825958654342816179" style="display:none">I think I personally enjoyed book 1 and 2 the most, but this one was incredibly powerful. Told in the perspective of Kristina's children almost 20 years later, Fallout shows us not only the long term effects of addiction, but also how wide the effects go. How many people and generation it touches. How many lives it marks. These kids all have deep rooted psychological issues caused by the simple fact of being born by an addict, but also by being abandoned, feeling unloved and alone. It was interesting to see how different these kids all turned out as well. My favorite perspective was Hunter's. I found his narrative to be the most compelling. This may simply be because his story most closely relates to the other books. We knew him as a baby, as well as the specifics surrounding his family situation from birth. It's like I felt more attached to him because of that.<br /><br />Also in this edition we get to hear from the real "Kristina". She writes of her addiction and how/why she went down that road. If you decide to buy this series make sure to get these editions. Each book has a special section that make the story all the more emotional just by reading of these real-life stories. The other 2 gave us bits of Ellen's very own journey from which the series is based on. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14825958654342816179" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/182743424?book_show_action=true">Jul 07, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joy Mo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joy Mo" href="/user/show/5754152-joy-mo">Joy Mo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer182743424" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14857668007738418032">I'm not quite sure what made me not like Fallout as much and the other Ellen Hopkins books. <br/><br/>Maybe<br/> it was that the characters all seemed to experience the same <br/> plot only with different people. <br/>I'm<br/> not quite sure, but I think it goes something like this: freakishly <br/> sensitive boy meets bland girl. They gawk at each other's<br/> perfection for a few sentences and then they have sexay tyme, eh,<br/> yes? But<br/>Just<br/> when you think they're ready to skip off into the sunset of meth<br/> and teen pregnancy, oooooooooooo</span>
  <span id="freeText14857668007738418032" style="display:none">I'm not quite sure what made me not like Fallout as much and the other Ellen Hopkins books. <br /><br />Maybe<br /> it was that the characters all seemed to experience the same <br /> plot only with different people. <br />I'm<br /> not quite sure, but I think it goes something like this: freakishly <br /> sensitive boy meets bland girl. They gawk at each other's<br /> perfection for a few sentences and then they have sexay tyme, eh,<br /> yes? But<br />Just<br /> when you think they're ready to skip off into the sunset of meth<br /> and teen pregnancy, ooooooooooooooooohs nooooooooooes! Turns out<br /> they just haven't quite ascended to the higher plain of <br />Sick<br /> -ening Maturity and/or Poetic Brooding after all! Apparently those <br /> wacky kids are human just like you and me, which provides them <br /> with plenty<br />of<br /> opportunities to feed <br />the <br /> monster in Ellen Hopkins' that survives <br /> on drama. This, of course, leads to many scenes in which <br /> Seth, Autumn and Summer<br />Angst<br /> -off for paragraphs on end, getting their wangst all over the <br /> reader. True, they do have real problems and their unhappiness is <br /> justified, but the things that happen to them seem contrived and <br /> like they were only put in to create (you guessed it) that funny <br /> thing called 'angst' that the young people these days seem so fond<br /> of. Also, a little thing that nagged me was Hopkins's apparent <br /> hate of foster homes. Yes kiddies, every foster dad is a molester <br /> and every foster mom is a distant bitch who lets it happen!<br /><br />That said,<br /> I didn't really hate Fallout.<br /> Sure it felt a little melodramatic at times,<br /> but the writing was addictive<br /> the portrayal of drugs and whatnot solid,<br /> and an overall worth-it <br /> trilogy-ender.<br />I only wish there was more Kristina,<br /> that wacky bitch. </span>

<div id="review_636642633" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/636642633" />
    <a title="Cailin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21141579-cailin"><img alt="Cailin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1389051296p2/21141579.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/636642633?book_show_action=true">Jun 08, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cailin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cailin" href="/user/show/21141579-cailin">Cailin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer636642633" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7336349343401145065">Ah, yes. Ellen Hopkins. You see, I'm a little late in the game here reading the Crank series. When I was in high school these books were extremely popular, therefore it was impossible to get them at the library. I'd read burned (more on that later) and detested it, so I put the Crank series at the very bottom of my "to read" list. <br/><br/>A few weeks ago, out of boredom, I finally read Crank and Glass. I liked them, I did. Went through them both in less than a day. It was only natural that I read Fallou</span>
  <span id="freeText7336349343401145065" style="display:none">Ah, yes. Ellen Hopkins. You see, I'm a little late in the game here reading the Crank series. When I was in high school these books were extremely popular, therefore it was impossible to get them at the library. I'd read burned (more on that later) and detested it, so I put the Crank series at the very bottom of my "to read" list. <br /><br />A few weeks ago, out of boredom, I finally read Crank and Glass. I liked them, I did. Went through them both in less than a day. It was only natural that I read Fallout next, right? Well, lets just say it is a day of my life I will never get back. <br /><br />For starters, I was initially intrigued at Hopkin's decision to tell the story from the POV of Kristina's oldest children. However, the entire story took a nose dive about 1/3 of the way through the book. I won't bother to give a summary here, but I will recount the elements of the story that bothered me the most.<br /><br />1.) All three children, Hunter, Autumn, and Summer (autumn and summer, really now?) were as deep as puddles. I found their cliche and contrived story lines made them all incredibly unlikeable. Instead of really delving into the seemingly traumatic childhoods each endured in their own right, they instead found themselves wrapped up in their own vanilla teenage romances. I was particularly bothered by how forgettable some of the main characters turned out to be, such as Autumn's boyfriend Bryce and Summer's ex Matt. For all I could tell they were essentially the same person. The character development is incredibly lazy here- the same could be said of the sisters themselves. Hunters story showed the greatest promise, yet the middle of the book was mainly him getting unjustifiably angry with the back and forth relationship with his girlfriend Nikki, who is portrayed as a brainless Barbie doll. The important parts of the story, such as Hunter meeting his father and Autumn discovering her siblings, are weakly played out in short bursts of verse in favor of lengthy pages about driving through various deserts. Literally.<br /><br />2.) The blatant sexist undertones in this book are incredibly disturbing to me. Hopkins practically glorifies the fact that many of her female characters suffer abuse at the hands of their respective male partners. At one point, Summer's beau Kyle forces her to have sex with him although she had just confessed to him that she had been sexually abused as a child, and at many points in the story he is aggressive with her and orders her around like a puppet. It is hard to believe that the "tougher/stronger" girl would go along with this. I was also mad to hear Hunter guilt-tripping his mom about being raped, insinuating that she "asked for it." I could really go on all day here about these kind of themes portrayed in the book. <br /><br />3.) Hopkins confuses throughout the whole book. The constant switching of POV's, for one, left me dizzy. Aside from that, however, is the revelation that Kristina's mother writes three fictional books in the story titled "Crank", "Glass", and "Fallout." This is even hard for me to explain- now, is Hopkins trying to tell us that this is an Inception kind of deal, a book within a book within a real life story? What is real and what is fake? She also makes it a point to mention several times what a "famous author" Kristina's mother is in the book- many a time an autographed copy of her latest book was the resolution of a mini crisis in the story. It was cheesy, as if Hopkins imagined herself to really be that big and made plenty of space for her ego between the pages of her book.<br /><br />4.) Finally, the loose ends. There were so many pointless plot twists thrown in here to shock or engage the reader, but they instead fell flat. The ending result of the entire story felt like something I would have written in a game of the Sims, to put it one way. Autumn's possible pregnancy? The siblings all meeting each other for the first time? NOPE! You get to make that all up on your own, folks. The endless blah blah blah crap I poured through all day lead to a rushed and soap-opera type ending. The only spoiler I can give you is that Kristina and Trey somehow remarry and live as happily ever after as they can. But really? Two volatile addicts with a terrifying and traumatic past are really going to last in a relationship together? And flaky selfish Kristina, who can't love anyone, is going to continue to abandon her children in favor of a dude. We also never find out how Autumn reacts to her parents being together again after they are absent from her life up until that point? <br /><br />I need to stop. I could be here all night typing the flaws and shortcomings, and yes, general sloppiness of this book until my eyes fall out of my skull. But I simply use up my 20,000 character limit and then some. This book was so bad that I went out of my way to find this site so I could review it. Like I said before, I liked Crank and Glass all right because it was more engaging, it had more soul. I kind of understand what Hopkins was going for with her final installment of the series, but it turned into a bleak, hopeless, and vapid piece of writing. Her idea could have come through in so many different ways, and it could have even held the potential of being a five star work of art. I am truly surprised to see how many perfect reviews it got, so maybe she got what she wanted out of Fallout- a cash cow of a follow up to please those readers with a taste for mindless Facebook type drama. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7336349343401145065" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_125452378" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/125452378" />
    <a title="Courtney" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1739351-courtney"><img alt="Courtney" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1343846657p2/1739351.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/125452378?book_show_action=true">Oct 09, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Courtney" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Courtney" href="/user/show/1739351-courtney">Courtney</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1739351-courtney?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1739351-courtney?shelf=teen-fiction">teen-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1739351-courtney?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1739351-courtney?shelf=addiction">addiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1739351-courtney?shelf=abuse">abuse</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1739351-courtney?shelf=novel-in-verse">novel-in-verse</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer125452378" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17922479940915809100">In classic fan-girl fashion, I put this on hold as soon as it was entered into our library's catalog. I've been avidly following Ellen's work ever since I read the first book of this series several years ago. While this is the end of the series, it serves as a reminder that there really is no end to addiction. Whereas the first two books follow Kristina through her devastating dance with addiction and relapse, this one takes place years later with her eldest children telling their stories. There</span>
  <span id="freeText17922479940915809100" style="display:none">In classic fan-girl fashion, I put this on hold as soon as it was entered into our library's catalog. I've been avidly following Ellen's work ever since I read the first book of this series several years ago. While this is the end of the series, it serves as a reminder that there really is no end to addiction. Whereas the first two books follow Kristina through her devastating dance with addiction and relapse, this one takes place years later with her eldest children telling their stories. There is Hunter, the child born in Crank and adopted by Kristina's parents (bolstered by the interesting element of dealing with his grandmother's author-celebrity status, which would indicate that he was familiar with her previous semi-autobiographical novels). Then there is Autumn, the "lost" daughter, living with her aunt and grandfather. Also living with OCD and panic attacks and soon to be confronted by a past she knows little about. Finally, there is Summer, jostled in and out of foster care, a notoriously dicey system. She gets a brief reprieve (?) from the system to live with her father and his girlfriend. <br />Three very different teens, dealing with complex emotional issues all derived from their mother's addiction to the monster meth. Emotionally raw and painfully realistic, the final installment to this tragic trilogy is a satisfying stopping place in one family's on-going saga of addiction and its collateral damage.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17922479940915809100" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1216626168" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1216626168" />
    <a title="Shannon (kitchandpages)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10961933-shannon-kitchandpages"><img alt="Shannon (kitchandpages)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1441470068p2/10961933.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1216626168?book_show_action=true">Mar 02, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shannon (kitchandpages)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shannon (kitchandpages)" href="/user/show/10961933-shannon-kitchandpages">Shannon (kitchandpages)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781442471801" href="/book/show/15801340-fallout">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1216626168" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1783421839195803097">Well, I finally took the plunge and read the final book in the Crank Trilogy. Fallout was tough to get through at times, but definitely needed after Glass. I still think Crank could have been a stand-alone, which is how the author had originally written it - but I understand the outcry for more of Kristina's story from the fans.<br/>The only thing I can say about Fallout to avoid spoilers is that the story takes places 19 years after the events of Crank and Glass and follows three different protagoni</span>
  <span id="freeText1783421839195803097" style="display:none">Well, I finally took the plunge and read the final book in the Crank Trilogy. Fallout was tough to get through at times, but definitely needed after Glass. I still think Crank could have been a stand-alone, which is how the author had originally written it - but I understand the outcry for more of Kristina's story from the fans.<br />The only thing I can say about Fallout to avoid spoilers is that the story takes places 19 years after the events of Crank and Glass and follows three different protagonists who are closely connected to Kristina, the main protagonist in the first two books. The new characters stories are all different, each with their own struggles and temptations, but ultimately connected.<br />I spend a large portion of the book getting to know the new faces and trying to keep all the side characters straight. There were a lot and we don't see them consistently, yet are expected to keep them all straight. I still am a bit fuzzy on a few of them but got the overall gist of it. And while I liked all the new leads, I think the book was too busy and would have been more effective with two instead of three.<br />I did like, however, that Ellen Hopkins told real and honest stories that made sense in the wake of what Kristina did in the first two books. If you are looking for sunshines and daisies and a story wrapped up in a cute little bow by the end, you will not like Ellen Hopkins' books. And if they were like that, considering the content she is writing about in this trilogy, they wouldn't be at all effective or authentic. Addiction is real for many people and families and it isn't pretty or easy.<br />I HIGHLY recommend this trilogy to all people, particularly anyone with family members or friends struggling with addiction or in recovery. Teenagers should read these books instead of sitting through DARE, because these books don't hold back and teach you what REALLY happens when you party with the Monster.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1783421839195803097" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a title="Nicole aka FromReading2Dreaming" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicole aka FromReading2Dreaming" href="/user/show/21825445-nicole-aka-fromreading2dreaming">Nicole aka FromReading2Dreaming</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21825445-nicole-aka-fromreading2dreaming?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21825445-nicole-aka-fromreading2dreaming?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21825445-nicole-aka-fromreading2dreaming?shelf=ya-fiction">ya-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21825445-nicole-aka-fromreading2dreaming?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21825445-nicole-aka-fromreading2dreaming?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1726924289" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer683841359434373656">MY GOODNESS THIS BOOK IS AMAZING!!! <br/><br/>The third, and final installment of the Crank series did not disappoint. It was phenomenal I must say, because it takes of on the perspective of the three children from who was the main character in the first two books. This installment not only illustrates how drug addiction can impact the children of an addict, but also the family.<br/><br/>As someone who has had a parent use drugs, I have to say the book paints an accurate picture of what some of the circumstances ma</span>
  <span id="freeText683841359434373656" style="display:none">MY GOODNESS THIS BOOK IS AMAZING!!! <br /><br />The third, and final installment of the Crank series did not disappoint. It was phenomenal I must say, because it takes of on the perspective of the three children from who was the main character in the first two books. This installment not only illustrates how drug addiction can impact the children of an addict, but also the family.<br /><br />As someone who has had a parent use drugs, I have to say the book paints an accurate picture of what some of the circumstances may include. From foster homes to being raised by a grandparent, the book covers it. <br /><br />Hopkins does an amazing job of flushing out all the characters, and catching the audience up on what they have missed in the 19 year gap since the second and third book.<br /><br />I have to say though my biggest critique is when the author changes to three different view points, but I have to say that at times one can get the characters mixed up. Or is it just me? Personally, I would have preferred three different books for each of the children, but alas it did not happen.<br /><br />I HIGHLY recommend this book to anyone who has ever struggled with drug addiction or has been impacted by it in some way. THIS BOOK WAS SO GOOD AND I CANNOT WAIT UNTILL I CAN GET MY HANDS ON MORE OF HOPKINS' BOOKS!!!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="683841359434373656" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2609254308" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Rae" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1864653-rae"><img alt="Rae" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602768420p2/1864653.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2609254308?book_show_action=true">Nov 30, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rae" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rae" href="/user/show/1864653-rae">Rae</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1864653-rae?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1864653-rae?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1864653-rae?shelf=bt-audiobook">bt-audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2609254308" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12211816413420402071">Check out this review and others on my blog: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://thriftybibliophile.com'>https://thriftybibliophile.com</a><br/><br/>Fallout by Ellen Hopkins is the third and final book in the Crank trilogy. Nineteen years after Kristina meets the monster, her children continue to pick up the pieces of their mom’s bad decisions.<br/><br/>I was so excited to read Fallout, and while it was good, it wasn’t nearly as engaging as Crank and Glass. Kristina is not front and center in Fallout. Instead, Hunter, Autumn, and Summer take the stage.<br/><br/>The perspective shifts bac</span>
  <span id="freeText12211816413420402071" style="display:none">Check out this review and others on my blog: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://thriftybibliophile.com">https://thriftybibliophile.com</a><br /><br />Fallout by Ellen Hopkins is the third and final book in the Crank trilogy. Nineteen years after Kristina meets the monster, her children continue to pick up the pieces of their mom’s bad decisions.<br /><br />I was so excited to read Fallout, and while it was good, it wasn’t nearly as engaging as Crank and Glass. Kristina is not front and center in Fallout. Instead, Hunter, Autumn, and Summer take the stage.<br /><br />The perspective shifts back and forth between the three children, and it’s apparent that the repercussions of Kristina’s monster has made an impact on each child. Between sex, drug use, and mental illness, each child battles to find their place in the world and to fill the void that their mother left behind.<br /><br />While I enjoyed reading about the children, I became invested in Kristina’s life and was hoping Fallout would continue to be told from her perspective. Because the book was divided into three characters’ lives, I had a hard time connecting with any one of them.<br /><br />The events in the story, based off of real people and events in Ellen Hopkin’s life, were interesting, though sad. One child drifts in and out of foster homes. Another struggles with OCD. And the other dabbles in drug use. Each of the siblings struggles in their own way.<br /><br />The trilogy ended in kind of a ho-hum way. I didn’t feel a whole lot of closure, but maybe when drug use is involved, it’s hard to find adequate closure.<br /><br />The narrators all did a fantastic job. They got into their characters and told the story from their perspectives in an engaging manner.<br /><br />I would still recommend this trilogy to others! I loved the first two books but was hoping for something a little different with the third book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12211816413420402071" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_117733955" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/117733955" />
    <a title="Reader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3710381-reader"><img alt="Reader" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/117733955?book_show_action=true">Aug 20, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Reader" href="/user/show/3710381-reader">Reader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3710381-reader?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3710381-reader?shelf=not-a-straight-white-male-author">not-a-straight-white-male-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3710381-reader?shelf=female-writers">female-writers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3710381-reader?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer117733955" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11506755060985670555">I was disappointed with this one. It seemed like the three main characters, Hunter, Autumn, and Summer, all had the same voice and sometimes I got the details of their story lines confused. The struggles Hopkins chose to focus on the most for these characters barely had anything to do with how their lives were affected by Kristina. Hunter's pages were filled with annoying drama between him and his girlfriend, while Summer spent all her time worrying about her new asshole boyfriend. Autumn was th</span>
  <span id="freeText11506755060985670555" style="display:none">I was disappointed with this one. It seemed like the three main characters, Hunter, Autumn, and Summer, all had the same voice and sometimes I got the details of their story lines confused. The struggles Hopkins chose to focus on the most for these characters barely had anything to do with how their lives were affected by Kristina. Hunter's pages were filled with annoying drama between him and his girlfriend, while Summer spent all her time worrying about her new asshole boyfriend. Autumn was the only one whose life was actively affected by her mother's addictions, because she constantly has panic attacks, a side effect of having to hear violent arguments between Kristina and Trey as a young toddler. <br /><br />While the other two's lives were also affected by Kristina's choices (especially Summer, who is constantly moving from foster home to foster home), all these struggles take backseats to their annoying love lives. I think this book could have been A LOT better if Hopkins had chosen to put more focus on Hunter's feelings when he met his father and on Summer's experiences living as a foster child. Their uninteresting boyfriend/girlfriend dramas should NOT have taken up so much space. I understand that they're teenagers and they have other things going on, but this series is about drug addiction, and this book was supposed to highlight how much drugs affect the families of addicts. Therefore if the main effect that Kristina's drug use has on Summer's life is that she has to move from home to home and deal with abusive foster parents, then this is what her story should be mostly about. Same thing with Hunter. Hopkins could have seriously spent a lot of time developing this character's feelings about his father and their relationship. But instead, she resolves it in literally one conversation between the two. Then she writes like 20+ pages (per chapter) about Hunter having sex with his girlfriend or cheating on his girlfriend and the consequences. He also seems to be somewhat of a recreational drug user. These would have been much more interesting (and relevant) things to explore.<br /><br />I also didn't like the ending. There were too many loose ends. What's going to happen with Autumn and her pregnancy? Why did Hopkins even choose to make this character get pregnant? It seems like a cheap stunt to me. I think Hopkins went into this book determined to make the ending a hopeless one and so she threw a bunch of bleak plot twists into the story and didn't bother to develop them. An alternate ending for Autumn could have been her feeling comfort in the fact that she has a boyfriend who loves her and not being so scared of "losing" her aunt. <br /><br />I also didn't like some of the messages in this book. I didn't like that Hunter's girlfriend forgave him for cheating on her. I didn't like that Hunter somewhat blames Kristina for getting raped and that Kristina is made to look like the unreasonable character for getting offended at that. I didn't like how absent Kristina was the entire time. I didn't like how similar the personalities of the three main characters were. I didn't like the extremely rushed ending; I don't know why Hopkins didn't bother to develop this more. She spent pages and pages describing insignificant things, so the least she could have done was give more details for the most important encounter in the entire book. It felt like a lazy resolution.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11506755060985670555" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1833772674" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1833772674" />
    <a title="Megan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21656454-megan"><img alt="Megan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601664183p2/21656454.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1833772674?book_show_action=true">Dec 13, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Megan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Megan" href="/user/show/21656454-megan">Megan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21656454-megan?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21656454-megan?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21656454-megan?shelf=read-2016">read-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1833772674" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14076365855852295166"><b>As interesting as the premise of this book is, it just doesn't live up to it.</b><br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7171876-fallout' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fallout</a> is the aftermath of Kristina's mistakes while she was addicted to meth. These mistakes just so happen to be the three children she had (all with different men).<br/><br/>We have Hunter, who is the son of Brendan. He's the host of a radio station. He has a girlfriend who he loves very, very much because she's hot. Even though he loves her, his faithfulness sometimes dissipates for no reason at all.<br/><br/>Then there's Summer. She </span>
  <span id="freeText14076365855852295166" style="display:none"><b>As interesting as the premise of this book is, it just doesn't live up to it.</b><br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7171876-fallout" rel="nofollow noopener">Fallout</a> is the aftermath of Kristina's mistakes while she was addicted to meth. These mistakes just so happen to be the three children she had (all with different men).<br /><br />We have Hunter, who is the son of Brendan. He's the host of a radio station. He has a girlfriend who he loves very, very much because she's hot. Even though he loves her, his faithfulness sometimes dissipates for no reason at all.<br /><br />Then there's Summer. She has been in foster home after foster home, and she knows better than to make friends. She's totally fine with moving because she's so used to it until she meets the perfect guy.<br /><br />Last is Autumn (such original names). She lives with her aunt and grandfather. Life is pretty good except for the fact that she has OCD. Everything falls apart when her aunt gets married and moves out (because you know, Autumn's happiness is all that matters). At least she has Bryce, the perfect boy!<br /><br />I'm sorry, but I literally can't make the descriptions of these characters sound interesting. They were <b>so flat and didn't have any complexity to them.</b> I couldn't tell Autumn and Summer apart half of the time, which is saying a lot considering their chapters were in different fonts and they had different living situations.<br /><br />The thing that bugged me the most about this book is the <b>blatant sexism.</b> When Bryce goes to have sex with Autumn, she tells him that she's scared because she has triggering memories involving men and sex. He pulls the "don't you love/trust me?" card and just inserts her. It's never even hinted at that it was rape, but it still made me extremely uneasy and I wasn't down with their relationship after that point in time.<br /><br />There's also Hunter, who must be the stupidest guy ever. Nikki is such a great girlfriend to him, and he is constantly blowing up over the smallest things and getting them in intense arguments. Then he cheats on her and gets mad when she sees someone else for while. WHAT? And this is a quote from the smarty himself:<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>Grandpa Scott: Even beyond my time in radio, there have been plenty of temptations over the years. I'm sure for your mom, too.<br />Hunter: Mom? Women are tempted?</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Thanks for your dumb thought, Hunter.<br /><br />Other than that, this book didn't really feel resolved at the end or like things got better throughout it. I see the characters making the same mistakes and fighting with their "perfect" partners over and over. I don't know, guys. This book just <b>left me feeling weird.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="14076365855852295166" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_707347429" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/707347429" />
    <a title="Rita" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3285400-rita"><img alt="Rita" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1388657592p2/3285400.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/707347429?book_show_action=true">Aug 30, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rita" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rita" href="/user/show/3285400-rita">Rita</a>

  <span id="freeText14881972096516193325" style="display:none">What a great ending to the trilogy!<br /><br />I did not expect that it would take me so damn long to read this novel, but work and school were very stressful and I didn't have time for anything. But taking me so long to read it did not mean that I haven't enjoyed reading this.<br /><br />I loved how the story took place twenty years after Kristina's demise with the monster. <br /><br />It is told from three different perspectives: Hunter, Autumn and Summer. They are three of her five kids and the story was about how Kristina's addiction affected them in several ways. <br /><br />It was gripping and authentic and I loved reading about all of the different characters. All of them had problems and they were trying to cope with those problems as well as with being a teenager and not having/having their mother in their life. <br /><br />The writing was great. I will definitely read more of Ellen Hopkins in the future. Her writing style is just too good not to read any more of it. <br /><br />Also her storywriting brings everything to the point and I love the rawness and authenticity of it.</span>

<div id="review_1665382249" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1665382249" />
    <a title="Daria Marshall" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21892859-daria-marshall"><img alt="Daria Marshall" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1450952957p2/21892859.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1665382249?book_show_action=true">Jan 21, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Daria Marshall" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Daria Marshall" href="/user/show/21892859-daria-marshall">Daria Marshall</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781442471801" href="/book/show/15801340-fallout">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21892859-daria-marshall?shelf=diverse-reads-2k17">diverse-reads-2k17</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21892859-daria-marshall?shelf=library-reads-2k17">library-reads-2k17</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21892859-daria-marshall?shelf=audiobook-reads-2k17">audiobook-reads-2k17</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1665382249" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11504351255478398506">4.5 stars<br/><br/>Fallout was way more powerful for me than Crank and Glass. But I think a lot of it has to do with the fact that the narration shifts to three of Kristina's children. As the child of an addict, I found myself sharing a lot of the same emotions and thoughts that Hunter, Autumn, and Summer had. <br/><br/>I thought that switching the narration was a smart move on Hopkins's part. It really shows just how far reaching the consequences of addiction can be. And I feel like we were still getting Kristina'</span>
  <span id="freeText11504351255478398506" style="display:none">4.5 stars<br /><br />Fallout was way more powerful for me than Crank and Glass. But I think a lot of it has to do with the fact that the narration shifts to three of Kristina's children. As the child of an addict, I found myself sharing a lot of the same emotions and thoughts that Hunter, Autumn, and Summer had. <br /><br />I thought that switching the narration was a smart move on Hopkins's part. It really shows just how far reaching the consequences of addiction can be. And I feel like we were still getting Kristina's story, so it felt like a good ending to the series.<br /><br />I felt like Hopkins did a good job of representing the panic attacks that Autumn feels. And I kind of liked that she also had OCD. I totally understood why she told Bryce that her parents were dead despite the fact that they weren't. When your parent is an addict and have pretty much abandoned you, sometimes it's easier to just pretend that they are dead. It makes it much easier to deal with the pain. But it's also hard to explain that sometimes. And while I get that Bryce was mad that she lied, I hate that he didn't give her a chance to really explain. I kinda wish that Hopkins hadn't added the possible pregnancy, but that's just me.<br /><br />Hunter was an interesting perspective to read since we've seen him in Crank and Glass, even though he was just a baby. I wish that we could have seen him and Brendan get to know each other a little more, especially since Brendan seems to have changed his life around after being in the armed forces. While I didn't like that he cheated on Nikki, I did kind of like that it helped bring him closer to Scott as he was asking him for advice on how to show Nikki he was sorry. And I'm glad that he really was sorry and did try to make it up to Nikki.<br /><br />Summer was interesting to read about, especially having her in the foster system. Her storyline was my least favorite, but it was still compelling. I wasn't the biggest fan of Kyle, but he grew on me and I did like their relationship. I also liked that Summer was willing to stand up for and protect her foster siblings when things went south. <br /><br />I also liked that at the end of the book, when everyone has finally re-connected, Kristina finally gets some closure and actually has an emotional breakdown (I know, that sounds harsh of me). And I totally understand why Hunter and Summer are having a hard time believing anything that Kristina is saying. Once you've heard enough lies, even the truth sounds like it. Especially coming out of the mouth of an addict. I think that this was a very strong conclusion to Kristina's story and I'm glad I stuck out reading the entire trilogy because I wasn't sure I would after Crank. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11504351255478398506" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_105495210" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/105495210" />
    <a title="Lori " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2630971-lori"><img alt="Lori " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1476872490p2/2630971.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/105495210?book_show_action=true">Jun 03, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lori " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lori " href="/user/show/2630971-lori">Lori </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Lori  by: </span>
      grumpybear17@msn.com
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2630971-lori?shelf=arc-for-review">arc-for-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2630971-lori?shelf=own-arc">own-arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer105495210" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13377354255355098740">I'm notorious for not reading blurbs to sequels. What's the point, because you already know you like the series! But sometimes this means I get surprises. Like with Fallout. At first I thought 'WHERE'S KRISTINA!!?' But after thinking about it I realized the genius behind the decision to make the book from Kristina's children's point of view. We all know that Kristina isn't going to get better. Not for a long time. So, Ellen Hopkins takes a big leap with this one and makes it 20 years after Glass</span>
  <span id="freeText13377354255355098740" style="display:none">I'm notorious for not reading blurbs to sequels. What's the point, because you already know you like the series! But sometimes this means I get surprises. Like with Fallout. At first I thought 'WHERE'S KRISTINA!!?' But after thinking about it I realized the genius behind the decision to make the book from Kristina's children's point of view. We all know that Kristina isn't going to get better. Not for a long time. So, Ellen Hopkins takes a big leap with this one and makes it 20 years after Glass. It worked flawlessly.<br /><br />These books never cease to amaze and horrify me. Since the main voices in this book weren't hopeless drug addicts it wasn't as horrifying. At least not from that angle. In Fallout we get a glimpse of the after effects. We see how Kristina's addiction affects everyone in her life and some people that will never even know her. Hunter, Autumn and Summer's voices come through so loud and clear. They have to deal with so many things, not having a mother, a predisposition to addiction, and all the regular teenage issues.<br /><br />Hopkins verse is as beautiful as always. This is the third book I have read by her now, and I'm still in awe of her talent. I don't know that I will ever be able to read another authors verse without comparing it to Ellen's. And I have found anyone else that stacks up yet.<br /><br />Overall, this was a great conclusion to the Crank trilogy. Most everything was wrapped up nicely or as nicely as you can expect from such a heartbreaking story. If you haven't read these books yet, I suggest you do so and soon!</span>
  <a data-text-id="13377354255355098740" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Bonnie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5136858-bonnie"><img alt="Bonnie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604440764p2/5136858.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/237922111?book_show_action=true">Nov 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bonnie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bonnie" href="/user/show/5136858-bonnie">Bonnie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5136858-bonnie?shelf=poetry-verse">poetry-verse</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5136858-bonnie?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer237922111" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10583631566143325413">Interested in more of my reviews? Visit my <a href='http://sweet-tidbits.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>blog</a>!<br/><br/>The final chapter in one of the most heart wrenching trilogies/series I’ve ever read. A truly emotional read and I believe a fabulous ‘ending’ although maybe ‘wrap-up’ would be a better description as the story is far from over. <br/><br/>In ‘Fallout’, Ellen Hopkins has switched up the point of view and timeline of the story. Set in the future, Kristina’s youngest son Hunter who was just a toddler in last book is now 19. The story is told from Hunter’s point</span>
  <span id="freeText10583631566143325413" style="display:none">Interested in more of my reviews? Visit my <a href="http://sweet-tidbits.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a>!<br /><br />The final chapter in one of the most heart wrenching trilogies/series I’ve ever read. A truly emotional read and I believe a fabulous ‘ending’ although maybe ‘wrap-up’ would be a better description as the story is far from over. <br /><br />In ‘Fallout’, Ellen Hopkins has switched up the point of view and timeline of the story. Set in the future, Kristina’s youngest son Hunter who was just a toddler in last book is now 19. The story is told from Hunter’s point of view, as well as Summer and Autumn’s: both Kristina’s children. By now Kristina has yet to fully get her life back on track and has 5 children all living with other family members or in foster care.<br /><br />I was a bit skeptical at this change and how well I would enjoy it after reading through Kristina’s eyes for the past books, but I was pleased at how well written it was. The multiple POV reminded me very much of Triangles; however, I had difficulty in differentiating between Summer and Autumn for at least the first half of the book. <br /><br />It was extremely intense ‘experiencing’ the impact Kristina had on each of her children. It was tragic, heartbreaking, and extremely painful to read about. Was it worth it? Yes. Ellen Hopkins has yet to disappoint and I continue to be amazed at how influential and powerful her books are.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10583631566143325413" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3013986341" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3013986341" />
    <a title="aPriL does feral sometimes " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes"><img alt="aPriL does feral sometimes " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1478243665p2/3409532.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3013986341?book_show_action=true">Oct 20, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="aPriL does feral sometimes " class="user" itemprop="url" name="aPriL does feral sometimes " href="/user/show/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes">aPriL does feral sometimes </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes?shelf=poverty-and-ignorance-suck">poverty-and-ignorance-suck</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes?shelf=illuminating">illuminating</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes?shelf=older-teen">older-teen</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3013986341" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1801821151101058125">'Fallout' by Ellen Hopkins is book three in a semi-autobiographical, mostly-fictional, story about the author's real-life daughter and her addiction to meth (methamphetamine). All three books are written in free verse. The first book is <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/270730.Crank__Crank___1_' title='Crank (Crank, #1) by Ellen Hopkins' rel='nofollow noopener'>Crank</a>. I think readers should start with the first book in the trilogy. <br/><br/>'Fallout' is the first novel in the series not written from main character Kristina Georgia Snow's point of view. Instead, we meet three of Kristina's five children - Hunter, Summer, Autumn. </span>
  <span id="freeText1801821151101058125" style="display:none">'Fallout' by Ellen Hopkins is book three in a semi-autobiographical, mostly-fictional, story about the author's real-life daughter and her addiction to meth (methamphetamine). All three books are written in free verse. The first book is <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/270730.Crank__Crank___1_" title="Crank (Crank, #1) by Ellen Hopkins" rel="nofollow noopener">Crank</a>. I think readers should start with the first book in the trilogy. <br /><br />'Fallout' is the first novel in the series not written from main character Kristina Georgia Snow's point of view. Instead, we meet three of Kristina's five children - Hunter, Summer, Autumn. None of them know much about each other because all of them live with either foster parents or relatives of the various men Kristina had sex with in order to score more meth. Some of the fathers went to prison, like Kristina, for possession and distribution, of course, so the kids are being passed around the relatives like they were products of defecation. All of the children have developed issues either because Kristina was using while she was pregnant or because she cared for them after their births as if they were single-use plastic bags. However, almost every family relative loves them dearly! However, many in the family are still battling their own addictions and/or poverty, and they have no or almost no ability or resources to parent their own children, much less Kristina's.<br /><br />Still, the kids are struggling to be normal in their various locations living with foster relatives and complete strangers - mainly through ego-boosting sex, desperate hook-ups and excessive alcohol use. They know how bad meth is, after all. But staying in school is hard when one is full of self-hate, no self-confidence, rage and anxiety disorders, and being ordered to move from relative to foster home or needing to sleep in a hook-up's car. Still, those kids who know Kristina was their mom still like to believe she loves them! -although she never visits or calls. The ones who do accidentally meet her here and there and know who she is are somehow not comforted by her hurried proclamations of undying mother love.<br /><br />Christmas is coming! Will there be a miracle?<br /><br /><br />The first two novels follow Kristina's disastrous fall into moral depravity. 'Fallout' is more about the teenage and young adult kids beginning to experience early milestone failures in their lives - from bad choices of lovers to a hopeless sense of making any effort to succeed - unable to fill the emptiness each has within their hearts and souls. The three kids have alternating chapters which are distinguished from each other by different fonts, but I think the fonts should have been more different. <br /><br />Although 'Fallout' is good enough, it seemed more unfocused, more muddled, to me than the previous two books in the series.<br /><br /><br />Below are the effects of using meth, per WebMD <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.webmd.com/mental-health/addiction/crystal-meth-what-you-should_know#2:">https://www.webmd.com/mental-health/a...</a><br /><br /><i>-Meth can make a user's body temperature rise so high he could pass out or even die.<br />A user may feel anxious and confused, be unable to sleep, have mood swings, and become violent.<br /><br />-Looks can change dramatically. A user may age quickly. His skin may dull, and he can develop hard-to-heal sores and pimples. He may have a dry mouth and stained, broken, or rotting teeth.<br /><br />-He may become paranoid. He may hear and see things that aren’t there. He may think about hurting himself or others. He may also feel as though insects are crawling on or under his skin.<br /><br />-A meth user is at higher risk for HIV/AIDS. The drug can affect judgment and lessen inhibitions. Someone under the influence of the drug may be more likely to engage in risky behaviors, such as unsafe sex.</i><br /><br /><br />These are the signs someone is using meth:<br /><br /><i>-Not caring about personal appearance or grooming<br />-Obsessively picking at hair or skin<br />-Loss of appetite and weight loss<br />-Dilated pupils and rapid eye movement<br />-Strange sleeping patterns -- staying up for days or even weeks at a time<br />-Jerky, erratic movements; twitching; facial tics; animated or exaggerated mannerisms; and constant talking<br />-Borrowing money often, selling possessions, or stealing<br />-Angry outbursts or mood swings<br />-Psychotic behavior, such as paranoia and hallucinations</i><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1801821151101058125" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3651733934" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3651733934" />
    <a title="Sea Carlson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/124864880-sea-carlson"><img alt="Sea Carlson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605731256p2/124864880.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3651733934?book_show_action=true">Nov 18, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sea Carlson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sea Carlson" href="/user/show/124864880-sea-carlson">Sea Carlson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3651733934" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1644865130925286589">I read Crank and Glass and I think that this book is the only one that needs a review. When I first read this book, I had never experienced a plot that eventually overlapped from multiple characters in literature - or at least - I had never read a book that built up the convergence of all of the stories throughout quite like this. I can relate very much to having a broken family, and how that molds you as a person, and this book is very good at representing the changes we all go through in life </span>
  <span id="freeText1644865130925286589" style="display:none">I read Crank and Glass and I think that this book is the only one that needs a review. When I first read this book, I had never experienced a plot that eventually overlapped from multiple characters in literature - or at least - I had never read a book that built up the convergence of all of the stories throughout quite like this. I can relate very much to having a broken family, and how that molds you as a person, and this book is very good at representing the changes we all go through in life and how abuse and neglect can shape who you become and how you handle things. I think Crank and Glass are made worth the read by this third book, and the story we've read so far has a bigger world than we initially understood. I initially read Crank and Glass because I was unfamiliar with Ellen Hopkins' writing style and was very enthusiastic when purchasing her books, but those titles didn't seem to matter to me as much until I reached this book. It's unfortunate that you have to read the other two to really get the level of investment needed for this book to hit home because I think it would be a great stand alone book if it had a prologue that explained what you needed to know. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1644865130925286589" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1852472851" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer9044393104835110814">I enjoyed this book, I listened to it in audio. The funny thing is that if I didn't know it was written in verse book, I wouldn't have guessed it in a million years. It reads as a normal book.<br/><br/>I liked that this book focused on the children born to a mother addicted to meth- their genetic struggles with mental illness, how different their lives are -one not knowing she has siblings, a young man coming to terms with the fact that he was born from a rape, one in foster care, another adopted by an au</span>
  <span id="freeText9044393104835110814" style="display:none">I enjoyed this book, I listened to it in audio. The funny thing is that if I didn't know it was written in verse book, I wouldn't have guessed it in a million years. It reads as a normal book.<br /><br />I liked that this book focused on the children born to a mother addicted to meth- their genetic struggles with mental illness, how different their lives are -one not knowing she has siblings, a young man coming to terms with the fact that he was born from a rape, one in foster care, another adopted by an aunt and another by grandparents. <br /><br />Its a great look at different kinds of families and how people are not obligated to love their biological family. The struggle some of us face to not be our parents, to not repeat their mistakes. </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('OAZT1Eznz9uSDlhDKQWTtkLKBmkFdgpXjAhXV0xGNjF2E6fqtlbMthYj2uAKHH0W2jca68KA7pMg/ZyCm6MxZQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('0Q6fSMzNGTrH3i9sFC7jLKoqCfCO4nR6mOdPDzPBhZKfG2t2NnwaV0Pzrc83Nw2MMtcVckkUkL40EoTa5CSCxg==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer9126109192684665853"><i>Ellen Hopkins</i> is the New York Times bestselling author of <i>Crank</i>, <i>Burned</i>, <i>Impulse</i>, <i>Glass</i>, <i>Identical</i>, <i>Tricks</i>, <i>Fallout</i>, <i>Perfect</i>, <i>Triangles</i>, <i>Tilt</i>, and <i>Collateral</i>. She lives in Carson City, Nevada, with her husband and son. Hopkin's Facebook, Twitter, Tumblr and Pinterest pages get thousands of hits from teens who claim Hopkins is the "only one who understands me", and she can be visited at ellenhopkin</span>
  <span id="freeText9126109192684665853" style="display:none"><i>Ellen Hopkins</i> is the New York Times bestselling author of <i>Crank</i>, <i>Burned</i>, <i>Impulse</i>, <i>Glass</i>, <i>Identical</i>, <i>Tricks</i>, <i>Fallout</i>, <i>Perfect</i>, <i>Triangles</i>, <i>Tilt</i>, and <i>Collateral</i>. She lives in Carson City, Nevada, with her husband and son. Hopkin's Facebook, Twitter, Tumblr and Pinterest pages get thousands of hits from teens who claim Hopkins is the "only one who understands me", and she can be visited at ellenhopkins.com. <br /><br />Like most of you here, books are my life. Reading is a passion, but writing is the biggest part of me. Balance is my greatest challenge, as I love my family, friends, animals and home, but also love traveling to meet my readers. Hope I meet many of you soon!</span>
